With this inner product, if $(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ is a local orthonormal frame for $TM$ and $(e^1, \ldots, e^n)$ is the corresponding dual coframe, then the collection of tensor fields $E_{i_1} \otimes \cdots \otimes E_{i_k} \otimes e^{j_1} \otimes \cdots \otimes e^{j_l}$ as all the indices range from $1$ to $n$ forms a local orthonormal frame for $T^{(k,l)}(T_pM)$. In terms of any (not necessarily orthonormal) frame, this fiber metric satisfies
\begin{equation}
\langle F, G\rangle = g_{i_1r_1} \cdots g_{i_kr_k} g^{j_1s_1} \cdots g^{j_ls_l} F_{j_1 \cdots j_l}^{i_1 \cdots i_k} G_{s_1 \cdots s_l}^{r_1 \cdots r_k}. \tag{2.16}
\end{equation}

If $F$ and $G$ are both covariant, this can be written
\[
\langle F, G\rangle = F_{j_1 \cdots j_l} G^{j_1 \cdots j_l},
\]
where the last factor on the right represents the components of $G$ with all of its
indices raised:
\[
G^{j_1 \ldots j_i} = g^{i_1 s_1} \cdots g^{j_i s_I} G_{s_1 \ldots s_I}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\textit{Proof.} Problem 2-11. $\square$

\section{The Volume Form and Integration}

Another important construction provided by a metric on an oriented manifold is a
canonical volume form.

The construction needs one notion that the development so far has not: an orientation of $M$
that varies smoothly from point to point. A choice of orientation of each tangent space
already singles out a form $dV_g|_x$ on each $T_x M$; what makes $x \mapsto dV_g|_x$ a
\emph{differential form}, rather than an unrelated family of forms, is exactly the smoothness
of that choice.

\begin{definition}[Smooth Orientation]
\label{def:smooth-orientation}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.IsSmoothOrientation}
\leanok
A \emph{pointwise orientation} of a smooth $n$-manifold $M$ is a choice of orientation $o_x$ of
the vector space $T_x M$ for each $x \in M$. It is \emph{smooth} if every $p \in M$ has an open
neighbourhood $u$ carrying a smooth local frame $(Y_1, \ldots, Y_n)$ for $TM$ that is
positively oriented throughout $u$: for every $x \in u$ the basis $(Y_1|_x, \ldots, Y_n|_x)$ of
$T_x M$ induces $o_x$. An \emph{oriented} Riemannian manifold is a Riemannian manifold together
with a smooth orientation.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Gram--Schmidt Preserves Orientation]
\label{lem:gram-schmidt-preserves-orientation}
\lean{InnerProductSpace.gramSchmidtOrthonormalBasis_orientation}
\leanok
Let $V$ be an $n$-dimensional real inner product space and let $b = (b_1, \ldots, b_n)$ be a
basis of $V$. Then the Gram--Schmidt orthonormalization of $b$ induces the same orientation of
$V$ as $b$ does.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
Write $u_i$ for the unnormalized Gram--Schmidt vectors and $\hat u_i = u_i / |u_i|$ for their
normalizations, so that $(\hat u_i)$ is the orthonormalization of $b$. The change of basis from
$b$ to $(\hat u_i)$ is triangular, and its determinant equals
$\prod_{i=1}^{n} \langle \hat u_i, b_i \rangle$.

Each factor is positive. Indeed the recursion defining $u_i$ subtracts from $b_i$ a combination
of $u_1, \ldots, u_{i-1}$, each of which is orthogonal to $u_i$; hence
$\langle u_i, b_i \rangle = \langle u_i, u_i \rangle = |u_i|^2$, and therefore
$\langle \hat u_i, b_i \rangle = |u_i|$. Since $b$ is linearly independent, $u_i \ne 0$ and so
$|u_i| > 0$.

The determinant of the change of basis is thus positive, and a change of basis with positive
determinant preserves orientation.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Existence of Oriented Orthonormal Frames]
\label{prop:oriented-orthonormal-frames}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.exists_orientedOrthonormalFrame_nhds}
\leanok
\uses{def:smooth-orientation,lem:gram-schmidt-preserves-orientation,prop:existence-orthonormal-frames,def:riemannian-metric}
Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian $n$-manifold with a smooth orientation $o$. Then every $p \in M$ has
an open neighbourhood $u$ carrying a smooth local frame $(Z_1, \ldots, Z_n)$ for $TM$ that is
both orthonormal and positively oriented at every $x \in u$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:smooth-orientation,lem:gram-schmidt-preserves-orientation,prop:existence-orthonormal-frames}
By Definition \ref{def:smooth-orientation} there are an open $u \ni p$ and a smooth local frame
$(Y_1, \ldots, Y_n)$ on $u$ that is positively oriented at every $x \in u$. Orthonormalize it
fibrewise: by Proposition \ref{prop:existence-orthonormal-frames} the resulting family
$(Z_1, \ldots, Z_n)$ is again a smooth local frame on $u$, orthonormal at every $x \in u$. By
Lemma \ref{lem:gram-schmidt-preserves-orientation}, applied in the inner product space
$(T_x M, g_x)$, the basis $(Z_1|_x, \ldots, Z_n|_x)$ induces the same orientation as
$(Y_1|_x, \ldots, Y_n|_x)$, which is $o_x$.

The initial-span condition of Proposition \ref{prop:existence-orthonormal-frames} is not by
itself enough here: $\operatorname{span}(Z_1|_x, \ldots, Z_k|_x) =
\operatorname{span}(Y_1|_x, \ldots, Y_k|_x)$ for every $k$ does not determine the orientation of
$(Z_i|_x)$, as replacing $Z_1$ by $-Z_1$ shows. This is why the orientation must be tracked
through the orthonormalization, by Lemma \ref{lem:gram-schmidt-preserves-orientation}.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[The Riemannian Volume Form]
\label{def:volume-form-pointwise}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.volumeForm}
\leanok
\uses{def:riemannian-metric,def:smooth-orientation}
Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian $n$-manifold and let $o$ be a pointwise orientation of $M$. For each
$x \in M$ let $dV_g|_x$ be the volume form of the oriented inner product space
$(T_x M, g_x, o_x)$, that is, the unique alternating $n$-form on $T_x M$ taking the value $1$ on
every orthonormal basis of $T_x M$ inducing $o_x$. The family $dV_g : x \mapsto dV_g|_x$ is the
\emph{Riemannian volume form} of $(M, g, o)$.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[The Determinant Formula]
\label{prop:volume-form-determinant}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.volumeForm_apply_eq_det}
\leanok
\uses{def:volume-form-pointwise,prop:oriented-orthonormal-frames}
Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian $n$-manifold with pointwise orientation $o$, let $(E_1,\ldots,E_n)$
be a local orthonormal frame on an open set $u$ that is positively oriented at $x \in u$, and let
$v_1, \ldots, v_n \in T_x M$. Then
\[
dV_g|_x(v_1, \ldots, v_n) = \det \bigl( \langle E_i|_x, v_j \rangle_g \bigr)_{i,j=1}^{n}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:volume-form-pointwise}
The tuple $(E_1|_x, \ldots, E_n|_x)$ is an orthonormal basis of $(T_x M, g_x)$ inducing $o_x$, so
by Definition \ref{def:volume-form-pointwise} $dV_g|_x$ is the determinant form of that basis.
The determinant form of an orthonormal basis $E$ sends $(v_1,\ldots,v_n)$ to the determinant of
the matrix expressing the $v_j$ in the basis $E$, whose $(i,j)$ entry is the coefficient
$\langle E_i|_x, v_j \rangle_g$ of $v_j$ along $E_i|_x$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[The Characterizing Property of $dV_g$]
\label{prop:volume-form-value-one}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.volumeForm_apply_eq_one}
\leanok
\uses{def:volume-form-pointwise,prop:oriented-orthonormal-frames}
Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian $n$-manifold with pointwise orientation $o$ and let
$(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ be a local orthonormal frame on an open set $u$ that is positively oriented
at $x \in u$. Then $dV_g|_x(E_1|_x, \ldots, E_n|_x) = 1$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:volume-form-pointwise}
Immediate from Definition \ref{def:volume-form-pointwise}: $(E_1|_x, \ldots, E_n|_x)$ is an
orthonormal basis of $T_x M$ inducing $o_x$, and $dV_g|_x$ takes the value $1$ on every such
basis. Equivalently, the matrix of Proposition \ref{prop:volume-form-determinant} is the
identity, whose determinant is $1$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Uniqueness of $dV_g$]
\label{prop:volume-form-uniqueness}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.volumeForm_unique}
\leanok
\uses{def:volume-form-pointwise,prop:volume-form-value-one}
Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian $n$-manifold with pointwise orientation $o$, let $(E_1,\ldots,E_n)$
be a local orthonormal frame on an open set $u$ that is positively oriented at $x \in u$, and let
$\theta$ be an alternating $n$-form on $T_x M$ with $\theta(E_1|_x, \ldots, E_n|_x) = 1$. Then
$\theta = dV_g|_x$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{prop:volume-form-value-one}
An alternating $n$-form on an $n$-dimensional space is determined by its value on a single
basis: every such form $\phi$ satisfies $\phi = \phi(E_1|_x,\ldots,E_n|_x) \det\nolimits_E$,
where $\det_E$ is the determinant form of the basis $(E_i|_x)$. Both $\theta$ and $dV_g|_x$ take
the value $1$ there, the latter by Proposition \ref{prop:volume-form-value-one}, so both equal
$\det_E$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Top-Degree Forms are Proportional]
\label{lem:top-forms-proportional}
\lean{ContinuousAlternatingMap.eq_smul_of_apply_basis_ne_zero}
\leanok
Let $V$ be an $n$-dimensional real vector space, let $b = (b_1, \ldots, b_n)$ be a basis of $V$,
and let $\omega$ and $\theta$ be alternating $n$-forms on $V$ with
$\theta(b_1, \ldots, b_n) \ne 0$. Then
\[
\omega = \frac{\omega(b_1, \ldots, b_n)}{\theta(b_1, \ldots, b_n)} \, \theta .
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
Every alternating $n$-form $\phi$ on $V$ satisfies $\phi = \phi(b_1,\ldots,b_n) \det\nolimits_b$,
where $\det_b$ is the determinant form of $b$. Applying this to $\theta$ and dividing by
$\theta(b_1,\ldots,b_n) \ne 0$ expresses $\det_b$ as a multiple of $\theta$; substituting that
into the same identity for $\omega$ gives the claim.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[The Wedge Product of Covectors]
\label{def:wedge-covectors}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.wedgeCovectors}
\leanok
Let $V$ be a real topological vector space and let $f_1, \ldots, f_n$ be continuous linear
functionals on $V$. Their \emph{wedge product} is the alternating $n$-form
\[
(f_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge f_n)(v_1, \ldots, v_n) = \det \bigl( f_i(v_j) \bigr)_{i,j=1}^{n} .
\]
This is alternating and multilinear in $(v_1, \ldots, v_n)$ because the determinant is
alternating and multilinear in the columns of its matrix, and it is continuous because a
determinant is a polynomial in the entries $f_i(v_j)$, each of which depends continuously on
$v_j$. This is the determinant convention for the wedge product, as used throughout.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[The Coframe Characterization of $dV_g$]
\label{prop:volume-form-coframe}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.volumeForm_eq_wedgeCovectors}
\leanok
\uses{def:wedge-covectors,def:volume-form-pointwise,prop:volume-form-determinant,prop:oriented-orthonormal-frames}
Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian $n$-manifold with pointwise orientation $o$, and let
$(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ be a local orthonormal frame on an open set $u$ that is positively oriented
at $x \in u$. Let $(e^1, \ldots, e^n)$ be the dual coframe, $e^i = \langle E_i, \cdot \rangle_g$.
Then
\[
dV_g|_x = e^1 \wedge \cdots \wedge e^n .
\]
This is characterization (a) of Lee's Proposition 2.41.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:wedge-covectors,prop:volume-form-determinant}
Both sides are alternating $n$-forms on $T_x M$, so it suffices to compare them on an arbitrary
tuple $(v_1, \ldots, v_n)$. By Definition \ref{def:wedge-covectors},
\[
(e^1 \wedge \cdots \wedge e^n)(v_1, \ldots, v_n)
  = \det \bigl( e^i(v_j) \bigr)_{i,j}
  = \det \bigl( \langle E_i|_x, v_j \rangle_g \bigr)_{i,j},
\]
which is $dV_g|_x(v_1, \ldots, v_n)$ by Proposition \ref{prop:volume-form-determinant}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[The Riemannian Volume Form is Smooth]
\label{prop:volume-form-smooth}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.contMDiff_volumeForm}
\leanok
\uses{def:volume-form-pointwise,def:smooth-orientation,prop:oriented-orthonormal-frames,lem:top-forms-proportional,prop:volume-form-determinant,prop:volume-form-value-one,lem:inner-product-vector-fields-smooth}
Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian $n$-manifold with a smooth orientation $o$. Then $dV_g$ is a smooth
$n$-form on $M$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{prop:oriented-orthonormal-frames,lem:top-forms-proportional,prop:volume-form-determinant,prop:volume-form-value-one,lem:inner-product-vector-fields-smooth}
Smoothness is local, so fix $x_0 \in M$. Choose a local trivialization $e$ of $TM$ over an open
set containing $x_0$ and write $e^{-1}_x : \mathbb{R}^n \to T_x M$ for the induced isomorphism of
the fibre over $x$. The trivialization of $TM$ induces one of the bundle of $n$-forms, under
which the value of $dV_g$ at $x$ is read as the $n$-form
$\Phi(x) = dV_g|_x \circ e^{-1}_x$ on $\mathbb{R}^n$; thus $dV_g$ is smooth at $x_0$ if and only
if $x \mapsto \Phi(x)$ is.

Fix once and for all a basis $b = (b_1,\ldots,b_n)$ of $\mathbb{R}^n$. By Proposition
\ref{prop:oriented-orthonormal-frames} there are an open $u \ni x_0$ and a smooth local frame
$(Z_1, \ldots, Z_n)$ on $u$, orthonormal and positively oriented at every $x \in u$.

First, $\Phi(x_0)(b_1,\ldots,b_n) \ne 0$. Indeed $dV_g|_{x_0}(Z_1|_{x_0},\ldots,Z_n|_{x_0}) = 1$
by Proposition \ref{prop:volume-form-value-one}, so $dV_g|_{x_0} \ne 0$; and
$(e^{-1}_{x_0} b_1, \ldots, e^{-1}_{x_0} b_n)$ is a basis of $T_{x_0} M$, because $e^{-1}_{x_0}$
is an isomorphism; and a nonzero alternating $n$-form cannot vanish on a basis, since by Lemma
\ref{lem:top-forms-proportional} its value on a basis determines it.

Since the $n$-forms on $\mathbb{R}^n$ form a line, Lemma \ref{lem:top-forms-proportional} applied
with $\theta = \Phi(x_0)$ now gives, for every $x$,
\[
\Phi(x) = \frac{\Phi(x)(b_1,\ldots,b_n)}{\Phi(x_0)(b_1,\ldots,b_n)} \, \Phi(x_0) .
\]
The right-hand side is a scalar function of $x$ times the fixed form $\Phi(x_0)$, so it suffices
to prove that $x \mapsto \Phi(x)(b_1,\ldots,b_n)$ is smooth at $x_0$.

By Proposition \ref{prop:volume-form-determinant}, for every $x \in u$,
\[
\Phi(x)(b_1,\ldots,b_n) = dV_g|_x \bigl(e^{-1}_x b_1, \ldots, e^{-1}_x b_n\bigr)
  = \det \bigl( \langle Z_i|_x, e^{-1}_x b_j \rangle_g \bigr)_{i,j=1}^{n} .
\]
For each fixed $j$ the assignment $x \mapsto e^{-1}_x b_j$ is a smooth local section of $TM$: it
is the local frame induced on $TM$ by the trivialization $e$ and the basis $b$, which is constant
in that trivialization. Each $Z_i$ is smooth on $u$ by construction. Hence each entry
$x \mapsto \langle Z_i|_x, e^{-1}_x b_j \rangle_g$ is smooth on $u$ by Lemma
\ref{lem:inner-product-vector-fields-smooth}. A determinant is a polynomial in the entries of
its matrix, so $x \mapsto \Phi(x)(b_1,\ldots,b_n)$ is smooth on $u$, and in particular at $x_0$.
\end{proof}

Characterization (c) of Proposition \ref{prop:riemannian-volume-form} computes $dV_g$ in oriented
local coordinates. It is proved for an arbitrary oriented local frame rather than only for a
coordinate frame: a coordinate frame $(\partial/\partial x^i)$ is a local frame, its matrix
$\bigl(g(\partial_i,\partial_j)\bigr)$ is Lee's $(g_{ij})$, and its dual coframe is $(dx^i)$, so
the general statement contains Lee's verbatim.

\begin{definition}[The Matrix of $g$ in a Frame]
\label{def:frame-matrix}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.frameMatrix}
\leanok
Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian manifold and $(Y_1,\ldots,Y_n)$ a local frame on an open set $u$. The
\emph{matrix of $g$ in the frame $(Y_i)$} at $x \in u$ is
\[
g_{ij}(x) = \langle Y_i|_x, Y_j|_x \rangle_g .
\]
For a coordinate frame $(\partial/\partial x^i)$ this is Lee's $(g_{ij})$.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[The Gram Determinant of a Frame is Nonzero]
\label{lem:frame-matrix-nonsingular}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.frameMatrix_det_ne_zero}
\leanok
\uses{def:frame-matrix}
With the notation of Definition \ref{def:frame-matrix}, $\det\bigl(g_{ij}(x)\bigr) \ne 0$ for
every $x \in u$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:frame-matrix}
The matrix $\bigl(g_{ij}(x)\bigr)$ is the Gram matrix of the family $(Y_1|_x,\ldots,Y_n|_x)$ with
respect to the inner product $\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_g$ on $T_x M$. A Gram matrix of a family
of vectors in an inner product space is nonsingular if and only if the family is linearly
independent. Since $(Y_i)$ is a frame, $(Y_i|_x)$ is a basis of $T_x M$, hence linearly
independent, and so $\det\bigl(g_{ij}(x)\bigr) \ne 0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[The Dual Coframe of a Frame]
\label{def:dual-coframe}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.dualCoframe}
\leanok
\uses{def:frame-matrix,lem:frame-matrix-nonsingular}
With the notation of Definition \ref{def:frame-matrix}, write $\bigl(g^{ij}(x)\bigr)$ for the
inverse of the matrix $\bigl(g_{ij}(x)\bigr)$, which exists by Lemma
\ref{lem:frame-matrix-nonsingular}. The \emph{dual coframe} of $(Y_i)$ is the family of covectors
\[
\varepsilon^i|_x = \sum_{j} g^{ij}(x) \, \langle Y_j|_x, \cdot \rangle_g .
\]
For a coordinate frame this is the coordinate coframe $(dx^i)$.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[The Dual Coframe is Dual]
\label{lem:dual-coframe-duality}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.dualCoframe_apply_frame}
\leanok
\uses{def:dual-coframe,def:frame-matrix}
With the notation of Definition \ref{def:dual-coframe}, $\varepsilon^i|_x(Y_k|_x) = \delta^i_k$
for all $i,k$ and all $x \in u$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:dual-coframe,def:frame-matrix,lem:frame-matrix-nonsingular}
By definition,
\[
\varepsilon^i|_x(Y_k|_x) = \sum_j g^{ij}(x) \, \langle Y_j|_x, Y_k|_x \rangle_g
  = \sum_j g^{ij}(x) \, g_{jk}(x),
\]
which is the $(i,k)$ entry of the product of $\bigl(g^{ij}(x)\bigr)$ with $\bigl(g_{ij}(x)\bigr)$.
Since the first matrix is by definition the inverse of the second, that product is the identity,
so the entry is $\delta^i_k$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[The Gram Determinant Formula, Pointwise]
\label{lem:volume-form-gram-determinant}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.volumeFormL_apply_eq_sqrt_det_gram}
\leanok
\uses{lem:gram-schmidt-preserves-orientation}
Let $V$ be an oriented $n$-dimensional inner product space with volume form $dV$, and let
$(b_1,\ldots,b_n)$ be a positively oriented basis of $V$, not assumed orthonormal. Then
\[
dV(b_1,\ldots,b_n) = \sqrt{\det\bigl(\langle b_i, b_j \rangle\bigr)} .
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{lem:gram-schmidt-preserves-orientation}
Let $(e_1,\ldots,e_n)$ be the Gram--Schmidt orthonormalization of $(b_i)$. By Lemma
\ref{lem:gram-schmidt-preserves-orientation} it is a positively oriented orthonormal basis. Let
$A$ be the matrix $A_{ij} = \langle e_i, b_j \rangle$, so that $b_j = \sum_i A_{ij} e_i$.

Expanding each $b_i$ in the orthonormal basis $(e_k)$ gives
\[
\langle b_i, b_j \rangle = \Bigl\langle \sum_k A_{ki} e_k, \sum_l A_{lj} e_l \Bigr\rangle
  = \sum_k A_{ki} A_{kj} = (A^{\mathsf T} A)_{ij},
\]
so $\det\bigl(\langle b_i, b_j\rangle\bigr) = \det(A^{\mathsf T}A) = (\det A)^2$.

By the determinant formula of Proposition \ref{prop:volume-form-determinant} applied to the
oriented orthonormal basis $(e_i)$, we have $dV(b_1,\ldots,b_n) = \det A$. Finally $\det A > 0$:
$\det A$ is the determinant of the change of basis from $(e_i)$ to $(b_j)$, and it is positive
exactly because the two bases induce the same orientation. Hence
$\sqrt{\det(\langle b_i,b_j\rangle)} = \sqrt{(\det A)^2} = |\det A| = \det A = dV(b_1,\ldots,b_n)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[The Value of $dV_g$ on an Oriented Frame]
\label{prop:volume-form-frame-value}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.volumeForm_apply_eq_sqrt_det_frameMatrix}
\leanok
\uses{def:volume-form-pointwise,def:frame-matrix,lem:volume-form-gram-determinant}
Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian $n$-manifold with a pointwise orientation, and let $(Y_1,\ldots,Y_n)$
be a local frame on $u$ that is positively oriented at $x \in u$. Then
\[
dV_g|_x(Y_1|_x, \ldots, Y_n|_x) = \sqrt{\det\bigl(g_{ij}(x)\bigr)} .
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{lem:volume-form-gram-determinant,def:frame-matrix}
Apply Lemma \ref{lem:volume-form-gram-determinant} to the oriented inner product space $T_x M$ and
its positively oriented basis $(Y_i|_x)$; the Gram matrix $\bigl(\langle Y_i|_x, Y_j|_x\rangle_g\bigr)$
is by Definition \ref{def:frame-matrix} the matrix $\bigl(g_{ij}(x)\bigr)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Lee 2.41(c): the Coordinate Formula for $dV_g$]
\label{prop:volume-form-coordinate-formula}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.volumeForm_eq_sqrt_det_smul_wedgeCovectors}
\leanok
\uses{def:volume-form-pointwise,def:frame-matrix,def:wedge-covectors,prop:volume-form-frame-value,lem:top-forms-proportional,lem:dual-coframe-duality}
Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian $n$-manifold with a pointwise orientation, let $(Y_1,\ldots,Y_n)$ be a
local frame on $u$ that is positively oriented at $x \in u$, and let $(\varepsilon^1,\ldots,
\varepsilon^n)$ be any coframe dual to it at $x$, that is $\varepsilon^i(Y_k|_x) = \delta^i_k$.
Then
\[
dV_g|_x = \sqrt{\det\bigl(g_{ij}(x)\bigr)} \; \varepsilon^1 \wedge \cdots \wedge \varepsilon^n .
\]
In particular, for oriented local coordinates $(x^1,\ldots,x^n)$, taking $(Y_i)$ to be the
coordinate frame $(\partial/\partial x^i)$ and $\varepsilon^i = dx^i$ gives
$dV_g = \sqrt{\det(g_{ij})}\, dx^1 \wedge \cdots \wedge dx^n$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{prop:volume-form-frame-value,lem:top-forms-proportional,def:wedge-covectors,lem:dual-coframe-duality}
Such a dual coframe exists, by Definition \ref{def:dual-coframe} and Lemma
\ref{lem:dual-coframe-duality}.

Both sides are $n$-forms on the $n$-dimensional space $T_x M$, and by Lemma
\ref{lem:top-forms-proportional} such a form is determined by its value on the single basis
$(Y_i|_x)$; so it suffices to check they agree there.

By Definition \ref{def:wedge-covectors},
\[
(\varepsilon^1 \wedge \cdots \wedge \varepsilon^n)(Y_1|_x,\ldots,Y_n|_x)
  = \det\bigl(\varepsilon^i(Y_j|_x)\bigr) = \det(\delta^i_j) = 1,
\]
so the right-hand side takes the value $\sqrt{\det(g_{ij}(x))}$ on $(Y_i|_x)$. The left-hand side
takes the same value by Proposition \ref{prop:volume-form-frame-value}.
\end{proof}

Lee's Proposition 2.41 collects the preceding results: its characterizations (a), (b) and (c) are
Propositions \ref{prop:volume-form-coframe}, \ref{prop:volume-form-value-one} and
\ref{prop:volume-form-coordinate-formula} respectively.

\begin{proposition}[The Riemannian Volume Form]
\label{prop:riemannian-volume-form}
\dcref{ch2:2.41}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.riemannian_volumeForm}
\leanok
\uses{def:volume-form-pointwise,prop:volume-form-smooth,prop:volume-form-value-one,prop:volume-form-uniqueness,prop:volume-form-determinant,prop:volume-form-coframe,def:wedge-covectors,prop:volume-form-coordinate-formula}
Let $(M, g)$ be an oriented Riemannian $n$-manifold with or without boundary. There is a unique $n$-form $dV_g$ on
$M$, called the \emph{Riemannian volume form}, characterized by any one of the following
three equivalent properties:

\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
\item If $(e^1, \ldots, e^n)$ is any local oriented orthonormal coframe for $T^* M$, then
$$dV_g = e^1 \wedge \cdots \wedge e^n.$$

\item If $(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ is any local oriented orthonormal frame for $TM$, then
$$dV_g(E_1, \ldots, E_n) = 1.$$

\item If $(x^1, \ldots, x^n)$ are any oriented local coordinates, then
$$dV_g = \sqrt{\det(g_{ij})} \, dx^1 \wedge \cdots \wedge dx^n.$$
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:volume-form-pointwise,prop:volume-form-smooth,prop:volume-form-uniqueness,prop:volume-form-coframe,prop:volume-form-value-one,prop:volume-form-coordinate-formula}
The form $dV_g$ is the one of Definition \ref{def:volume-form-pointwise}, which is defined at each
point as the volume form of the oriented inner product space $T_x M$; it is a smooth $n$-form by
Proposition \ref{prop:volume-form-smooth}, and it is the unique $n$-form with property (b) by
Proposition \ref{prop:volume-form-uniqueness}, since an $n$-form on an $n$-dimensional space is
determined by its value on one basis.

Properties (a), (b) and (c) hold for it by Propositions \ref{prop:volume-form-coframe},
\ref{prop:volume-form-value-one} and \ref{prop:volume-form-coordinate-formula} respectively.

The three are equivalent because each pins the form down on a single basis: a form satisfying (a)
or (c) takes the value $1$ on an oriented orthonormal frame, since by Definition
\ref{def:wedge-covectors} a wedge of a dual coframe evaluates on the dual frame to
$\det(\delta^i_j) = 1$, and $\det(g_{ij}) = 1$ for an orthonormal frame; so each of (a) and (c)
implies (b), and (b) determines the form uniquely by Proposition
\ref{prop:volume-form-uniqueness}.
\end{proof}

The significance of the Riemannian volume form is that it allows us to integrate
functions on an oriented Riemannian manifold, not just differential forms. If $f$ is
a continuous, compactly supported real-valued function on an oriented Riemannian
$n$-manifold $(M, g)$ with or without boundary, then $f \, dV_g$ is a compactly supported
$n$-form. Therefore, the integral $\int_M f \, dV_g$ makes sense, and we define it to be the
\emph{integral of $f$ over $M$}. Similarly, if $M$ is compact, the \emph{volume of $M$} is defined to
be
$$\operatorname{Vol}(M) = \int_M dV_g = \int_M 1 \, dV_g.$$

In particular, if $D \subseteq M$ is a \emph{regular domain} (a closed, embedded codimension-$0$
submanifold with boundary), we can apply these definitions to $D$ with its induced
metric and thereby make sense of the integral of $f$ over $D$ and, in case $D$ is compact, the volume of $D$.

The notation $dV_g$ is chosen to emphasize the similarity of the integral $\int_M f \, dV_g$
with the standard integral of a function over an open subset of $\mathbb{R}^n$. It is \emph{not} meant
to imply that $dV_g$ is an exact form; in fact, if $M$ is a compact oriented manifold
without boundary, then $dV_g$ is never exact, because its integral over $M$ is positive, and exact forms integrate to zero by Stokes's theorem.

Because there are two conventions in common use for the wedge product (see p.~401), it should be noted that properties (a) and (c) of Proposition 2.41 are the same regardless of which convention is used; but property (b) holds only for the determinant convention that we use. If the Alt convention is used, the number 1 should be replaced by $1/n!$ in that formula.

Stating Exercise \ref{exer:isometry-preserves-volume-form} requires the pullback of a differential
form along a smooth map.

\begin{definition}[The Pullback of a Differential Form]
\label{def:pullback-alternating}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.pullbackAlternating}
\leanok
Let $\varphi : M \to \tilde{M}$ be a smooth map and $w$ a $k$-form on $\tilde{M}$. The
\emph{pullback} $\varphi^* w$ is the $k$-form on $M$ given at $x$ by
\[
(\varphi^* w)|_x(v_1,\ldots,v_k) = w|_{\varphi(x)}\bigl(d\varphi_x(v_1), \ldots, d\varphi_x(v_k)\bigr).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[A Metric-Preserving Map Pushes Orthonormal Frames Forward]
\label{lem:orthonormal-pushforward}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.IsMetricPreserving.orthonormal_pushforward}
\leanok
\uses{def:metric-preserving}
Let $\varphi : (M,g) \to (\tilde{M},\tilde{g})$ be metric-preserving and let $(E_i)$ be a
$g$-orthonormal frame on an open set $u$. Then for every $x \in u$ the family
$\bigl(d\varphi_x(E_i|_x)\bigr)$ is $\tilde{g}$-orthonormal.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:metric-preserving}
By the defining property of a metric-preserving map,
$\langle d\varphi_x v, d\varphi_x w \rangle_{\tilde{g}} = \langle v, w \rangle_g$ for all
$v,w \in T_x M$. Applying this to $v = E_i|_x$ and $w = E_j|_x$ gives
$\langle d\varphi_x E_i|_x, d\varphi_x E_j|_x \rangle_{\tilde{g}} = \langle E_i|_x, E_j|_x\rangle_g
= \delta_{ij}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[The Pushforward Frame is a Basis]
\label{lem:push-basis}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.IsMetricPreserving.pushBasis}
\leanok
\uses{lem:orthonormal-pushforward}
In the situation of Lemma \ref{lem:orthonormal-pushforward}, the family
$\bigl(d\varphi_x(E_i|_x)\bigr)$ is a basis of $T_{\varphi(x)}\tilde{M}$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{lem:orthonormal-pushforward}
An orthonormal family is linearly independent, so by Lemma \ref{lem:orthonormal-pushforward} the
family $\bigl(d\varphi_x(E_i|_x)\bigr)$ is linearly independent. It has $n$ members, and
$\dim T_{\varphi(x)}\tilde{M} = n$, so a linearly independent family of $n$ vectors in an
$n$-dimensional space spans, hence is a basis.
\end{proof}

\begin{exercise}\label{exer:isometry-preserves-volume-form}\dcref{ch2:2.42}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.IsMetricPreserving.pullbackAlternating_volumeForm}
\leanok
\uses{def:pullback-alternating,def:volume-form-pointwise,prop:volume-form-uniqueness,prop:volume-form-value-one,lem:orthonormal-pushforward,lem:push-basis}
Suppose $(M,g)$ and $(\tilde{M},\tilde{g})$ are oriented Riemannian manifolds, and $\varphi: M \to \tilde{M}$ is an orientation-preserving isometry. Prove that $\varphi^* dV_{\tilde{g}} = dV_g$.
\end{exercise}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:pullback-alternating,prop:volume-form-uniqueness,prop:volume-form-value-one,lem:orthonormal-pushforward,lem:push-basis}
Fix $x \in M$ and let $(E_1,\ldots,E_n)$ be a local oriented orthonormal frame near $x$. By
Definition \ref{def:pullback-alternating},
\[
(\varphi^* dV_{\tilde{g}})|_x(E_1|_x,\ldots,E_n|_x)
  = dV_{\tilde{g}}|_{\varphi(x)}\bigl(d\varphi_x E_1|_x, \ldots, d\varphi_x E_n|_x\bigr).
\]
By Lemmas \ref{lem:orthonormal-pushforward} and \ref{lem:push-basis} the family
$\bigl(d\varphi_x E_i|_x\bigr)$ is an orthonormal basis of $T_{\varphi(x)}\tilde{M}$, and it is
positively oriented because $\varphi$ is orientation-preserving. So by Proposition
\ref{prop:volume-form-value-one} the right-hand side equals $1$.

Thus $(\varphi^* dV_{\tilde{g}})|_x$ is an $n$-form taking the value $1$ on the oriented
orthonormal frame $(E_i|_x)$. By Proposition \ref{prop:volume-form-uniqueness} the only such
$n$-form is $dV_g|_x$, so $(\varphi^* dV_{\tilde{g}})|_x = dV_g|_x$. As $x$ was arbitrary,
$\varphi^* dV_{\tilde{g}} = dV_g$.
\end{proof}

For Riemannian hypersurfaces, we have the following important characterization of the volume form on the hypersurface in terms of that of the ambient manifold. If $X$ is a vector field and $\mu$ is a differential form, recall that $X \lrcorner \mu$ denotes \emph{interior multiplication} of $\mu$ by $X$ (see p.~401).

\begin{definition}[Interior Multiplication]
\label{def:interior-multiplication}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.camContract}
\leanok
Let $V$ be a real topological vector space and let $\mu$ be an alternating $(k+1)$-form on $V$.
For $x \in V$, the \emph{interior multiplication} $x \lrcorner \mu$ is the alternating $k$-form
\[
  (x \lrcorner \mu)(v_1, \ldots, v_k) = \mu(x, v_1, \ldots, v_k).
\]
It is alternating because $\mu$ is: if $v_i = v_j$ with $i \ne j$, then the tuple
$(x, v_1, \ldots, v_k)$ has two equal entries. It is continuous because $\mu$ is and
$(v_1,\ldots,v_k) \mapsto (x, v_1, \ldots, v_k)$ is.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Unit Normal]
\label{def:unit-normal}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.IsUnitNormalAt}
\leanok
\uses{def:normal-space}
Let $(\tilde M, \tilde g)$ be a Riemannian manifold and let $F : M \to \tilde M$ present $M$ as a
smooth immersion. A family $N$ assigning to each $x \in M$ a vector $N_x \in T_{F(x)}\tilde M$ is
a \emph{unit normal} at $x$ if
\[
  \tilde g_{F(x)}(N_x, dF_x v) = 0 \quad\text{for every } v \in T_x M,
  \qquad \tilde g_{F(x)}(N_x, N_x) = 1,
\]
that is, if $N_x \in N_x M$ and $|N_x|_{\tilde g} = 1$.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[The Adapted Frame Along a Hypersurface]
\label{lem:adapted-frame-cons-normal}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.inner_consNormal}
\leanok
\uses{def:unit-normal,def:metric-preserving,def:normal-space}
Let $(\tilde M, \tilde g)$ be a Riemannian $(n+1)$-manifold, let $F : M \to \tilde M$ present the
$n$-manifold $M$ as a smooth immersion, and let $g$ be a metric on $M$ that $F$ preserves. Let
$N$ be a unit normal at $x \in M$ and let $(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ be a $g$-orthonormal basis of
$T_x M$. Then
\[
  \bigl(N_x, dF_x E_1, \ldots, dF_x E_n\bigr)
\]
is a $\tilde g$-orthonormal family in $T_{F(x)}\tilde M$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:unit-normal,def:metric-preserving}
There are four cases. First, $\tilde g(N_x, N_x) = 1$ because $N$ is a unit normal. Second,
$\tilde g(N_x, dF_x E_i) = 0$ for each $i$, because $N_x$ is normal and $dF_x E_i$ is tangent to
$M$; the same holds with the arguments exchanged, by symmetry of $\tilde g$. Third, for $i, j$,
\[
  \tilde g_{F(x)}(dF_x E_i, dF_x E_j) = g_x(E_i, E_j) = \delta_{ij},
\]
the first equality because $F$ preserves the metric and the second because $(E_i)$ is
orthonormal. So the family is orthonormal.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[The Adapted Frame is an Ambient Basis]
\label{lem:adapted-frame-ambient-basis}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.consNormalBasis}
\leanok
\uses{lem:adapted-frame-cons-normal}
In the situation of Lemma \ref{lem:adapted-frame-cons-normal}, the family
$\bigl(N_x, dF_x E_1, \ldots, dF_x E_n\bigr)$ is a basis of $T_{F(x)}\tilde M$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{lem:adapted-frame-cons-normal}
By Lemma \ref{lem:adapted-frame-cons-normal} the family is orthonormal, hence linearly
independent. It has $n+1$ members and $\dim T_{F(x)}\tilde M = n+1$, so a linearly independent
family of $n+1$ vectors in an $(n+1)$-dimensional space spans, hence is a basis.
\end{proof}

For Riemannian hypersurfaces, we have the following important characterization of the volume form on the hypersurface in terms of that of the ambient manifold.

\begin{proposition}[Equation (2.17)]
\label{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-formula}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.volumeForm_eq_normalRestrict}
\leanok
\uses{def:interior-multiplication,def:unit-normal,lem:adapted-frame-cons-normal,lem:adapted-frame-ambient-basis,def:volume-form-pointwise,prop:volume-form-uniqueness,prop:volume-form-value-one,def:metric-preserving}
Let $(\tilde M, \tilde g)$ be an oriented Riemannian $(n+1)$-manifold, let $F : M \to \tilde M$
present the $n$-manifold $M$ as a smooth immersion, let $g$ be a metric on $M$ that $F$
preserves, and let $N$ be a unit normal at $x \in M$. Suppose $(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ is a local
oriented $g$-orthonormal frame near $x$ for which the adapted basis
$\bigl(N_x, dF_x E_1, \ldots, dF_x E_n\bigr)$ of $T_{F(x)}\tilde M$ is positively oriented. Then
\begin{equation}
dV_g|_x = \bigl((N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde{g}})|_M\bigr)_x, \tag{2.17}
\end{equation}
where the right-hand side is the $n$-form $(v_1, \ldots, v_n) \mapsto
dV_{\tilde g}|_{F(x)}(N_x, dF_x v_1, \ldots, dF_x v_n)$ on $T_x M$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:interior-multiplication,lem:adapted-frame-cons-normal,lem:adapted-frame-ambient-basis,prop:volume-form-uniqueness,prop:volume-form-value-one}
Evaluate the right-hand side on the frame $(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$: by definition of interior
multiplication and of the restriction, it equals
\[
  dV_{\tilde g}|_{F(x)}\bigl(N_x, dF_x E_1, \ldots, dF_x E_n\bigr).
\]
By Lemmas \ref{lem:adapted-frame-cons-normal} and \ref{lem:adapted-frame-ambient-basis} the
family $\bigl(N_x, dF_x E_1, \ldots, dF_x E_n\bigr)$ is an orthonormal basis of
$T_{F(x)}\tilde M$, and it is positively oriented by hypothesis. So by Proposition
\ref{prop:volume-form-value-one} the value is $1$.

Thus the right-hand side is an $n$-form on $T_x M$ taking the value $1$ on the oriented
orthonormal frame $(E_i|_x)$. By Proposition \ref{prop:volume-form-uniqueness} the only such
$n$-form is $dV_g|_x$, which is (2.17).
\end{proof}

The orientation hypothesis of Proposition \ref{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-formula} is not an
extra assumption on $M$: a unit normal produces, with no choices, the orientation that satisfies
it. The construction rests on the observation that an orientation of an $n$-dimensional space
\emph{is} a ray of nonzero $n$-forms, so a nonvanishing $n$-form orients the space outright.

\begin{lemma}[A Nonvanishing Top Form Orients the Space]
\label{lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.rayOfNeZero_eq_basis_orientation_iff}
\leanok
Let $V$ be an $n$-dimensional real vector space and let $\omega$ be a nonzero alternating
$n$-form on $V$. Then $\omega$ determines an orientation of $V$, namely the ray of $\omega$ in
the one-dimensional space of $n$-forms, and a basis $(b_1, \ldots, b_n)$ of $V$ is positively
oriented for it if and only if $\omega(b_1, \ldots, b_n) > 0$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
Every $n$-form on $V$ is a scalar multiple of the determinant form $\det{}_b$ of $b$; applying
the relation $\omega = c \cdot \det_b$ to $b$ itself and using $\det_b(b) = 1$ identifies the
scalar as $c = \omega(b)$, and $c \ne 0$ because $\omega \ne 0$. The orientation determined by
$b$ is the ray of $\det_b$, so the ray of $\omega = \omega(b) \cdot \det_b$ equals it exactly
when the scalar $\omega(b)$ is positive.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[The Orientation Induced by a Unit Normal]
\label{def:induced-orientation}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.inducedOrientation}
\leanok
\uses{def:unit-normal,def:interior-multiplication,lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation,lem:adapted-frame-ambient-basis,def:volume-form-pointwise}
In the situation of Proposition \ref{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-formula}, let $N$ be a unit
normal at every point of $M$. The \emph{induced orientation} of $M$ assigns to each $x \in M$ the
orientation of $T_x M$ determined, by Lemma \ref{lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation}, by the
$n$-form $\bigl((N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x$.

This is well defined: the form does not vanish, since its value on a $g$-orthonormal basis
$(E_i)$ of $T_x M$ is $dV_{\tilde g}(N_x, dF E_1, \ldots, dF E_n) = \pm 1$, the adapted family
being an orthonormal basis of $T_{F(x)}\tilde M$ by Lemma
\ref{lem:adapted-frame-ambient-basis}.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[The Induced Orientation is Lee's]
\label{lem:induced-orientation-characterization}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.consNormalBasis_orientation_eq_iff}
\leanok
\uses{def:induced-orientation,lem:adapted-frame-ambient-basis,lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation,prop:volume-form-value-one}
Let $(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ be a $g$-orthonormal basis of $T_x M$. Then $(E_i)$ is positively
oriented for the induced orientation of $M$ if and only if the adapted basis
$\bigl(N_x, dF E_1, \ldots, dF E_n\bigr)$ is positively oriented in $\tilde M$.

That is, the induced orientation is exactly the one Lee describes.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:induced-orientation,lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation,prop:volume-form-value-one}
By Lemma \ref{lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation}, $(E_i)$ is positively oriented for the
induced orientation if and only if
\[
  \bigl((N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x(E_1, \ldots, E_n)
    = dV_{\tilde g}\bigl(N_x, dF E_1, \ldots, dF E_n\bigr) > 0.
\]
The adapted family is an orthonormal basis of $T_{F(x)}\tilde M$, so by Proposition
\ref{prop:volume-form-value-one} the right-hand side is $1$ if that basis is positively oriented
and $-1$ if it is not. So the value is positive exactly when the adapted basis is positively
oriented.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Top Forms are Determined by One Basis]
\label{lem:top-form-eq-of-basis}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.eq_of_apply_basis}
\leanok
Let $V$ be an $n$-dimensional real vector space and let $b$ be a basis of $V$. If two alternating
$n$-forms on $V$ agree on $b$, they are equal.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
Each $n$-form $\theta$ satisfies $\theta = \theta(b) \cdot \det_b$, so two forms agreeing on $b$
are the same multiple of $\det_b$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Equation (2.17) for the Induced Orientation]
\label{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-induced}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.volumeForm_inducedOrientation_eq_normalRestrict}
\leanok
\uses{def:induced-orientation,lem:induced-orientation-characterization,lem:top-form-eq-of-basis,prop:volume-form-value-one,def:interior-multiplication,def:unit-normal}
Let $(\tilde M, \tilde g)$ be an oriented Riemannian $(n+1)$-manifold, let $F : M \to \tilde M$
present the $n$-manifold $M$ as a smooth immersion, let $g$ be a metric on $M$ that $F$
preserves, and let $N$ be a unit normal at every point of $M$. Then, for the induced orientation
of $M$,
\[
  dV_g = (N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde{g}})|_M
\]
at every point, with no compatibility hypothesis between the orientations of $M$ and $\tilde M$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:induced-orientation,lem:induced-orientation-characterization,lem:top-form-eq-of-basis,prop:volume-form-value-one}
Fix $x \in M$ and choose a $g$-orthonormal basis $(E_i)$ of $T_x M$. By Lemma
\ref{lem:top-form-eq-of-basis} it suffices to see that both sides agree on $(E_i)$.

Suppose first that $(E_i)$ is positively oriented for the induced orientation. Then
$dV_g(E_1,\ldots,E_n) = 1$ by Proposition \ref{prop:volume-form-value-one}, and by Lemma
\ref{lem:induced-orientation-characterization} the adapted basis is positively oriented in
$\tilde M$, so $(N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M$ also takes the value $1$ on $(E_i)$.

Otherwise $(E_i)$ is negatively oriented, and $dV_g(E_1,\ldots,E_n) = -1$; by Lemma
\ref{lem:induced-orientation-characterization} the adapted basis is then negatively oriented in
$\tilde M$, so $(N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M$ takes the value $-1$ on $(E_i)$ as well. In both
cases the two forms agree on $(E_i)$, hence are equal.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Smoothness of a Pulled-Back Section]
\label{lem:pullback-comp-section}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.contMDiffAt_comp_section}
\leanok
\uses{lem:ambient-tangent-bundle-riemannian}
Let $F : M \to \tilde M$ be a smooth map and let $Z$ be a smooth section of $T\tilde M$ defined
near $F(x_0)$. Then $x \mapsto Z_{F(x)}$ is a smooth section of the ambient tangent bundle
$F^* T\tilde M$ near $x_0$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{lem:ambient-tangent-bundle-riemannian}
The fibre of $F^* T\tilde M$ at $x$ is $T_{F(x)}\tilde M$, and a local trivialization of
$F^* T\tilde M$ near $x_0$ is by definition a local trivialization of $T\tilde M$ near $F(x_0)$
precomposed with $F$. Read in these trivializations the section in question is $Z$, read in the
trivialization of $T\tilde M$, composed with $F$. Both are smooth, hence so is the composite.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Smoothness of an Ambient Family at a Point]
\label{def:smooth-normal-at}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.IsSmoothNormalAt}
\leanok
\uses{lem:ambient-tangent-bundle-riemannian}
Let $F : M \to \tilde M$ present $M$ as a smooth immersion in a Riemannian manifold
$(\tilde M, \tilde g)$, and let $N$ assign to each $x \in M$ a vector $N_x \in T_{F(x)}\tilde M$.
Then $N$ \emph{varies smoothly at} $x_0 \in M$ if it is a smooth section of the ambient tangent
bundle $F^* T\tilde M$ at $x_0$.

The notion is pointwise rather than global because the normal fields it is applied to are in
general only defined and smooth on a neighbourhood.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Smooth Unit Normal Field]
\label{def:smooth-unit-normal-field}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.IsSmoothNormalField}
\leanok
\uses{def:unit-normal,def:smooth-normal-at,lem:ambient-tangent-bundle-riemannian,def:normal-space}
In the situation of Definition \ref{def:smooth-normal-at}, the family $N$ \emph{varies smoothly}
if it varies smoothly at every point of $M$. A \emph{smooth global unit normal field} for $M$ is
such a family that is in addition a unit normal at every point of $M$.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Negating One Member of a Local Frame]
\label{lem:frame-neg-member}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.isLocalFrameOn_negMember}
\leanok
Let $(Y_i)_{i \in \iota}$ be a smooth local frame for a smooth vector bundle $V \to B$ over an
open set $u \subseteq B$, and fix an index $i_0 \in \iota$. Then the family obtained from $(Y_i)$
by replacing $Y_{i_0}$ with $-Y_{i_0}$ is again a smooth local frame for $V$ over $u$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
The modified family is smooth because negation is a smooth bundle map. At each $x \in u$ it is
obtained from the basis $(Y_i|_x)$ of $V_x$ by scaling one member by the unit $-1$, so it is
linearly independent. Finally $-Y_{i_0}|_x$ and $Y_{i_0}|_x$ span the same line, so the modified
family spans the same subspace as $(Y_i|_x)$, namely all of $V_x$. Being independent and
spanning at every $x \in u$, it is a local frame.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[The Adapted Frame Varies Smoothly]
\label{lem:adapted-frame-smooth}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.contMDiffAt_consNormal}
\leanok
\uses{def:smooth-normal-at,lem:pushforward-smooth,def:unit-normal,lem:ambient-tangent-bundle-riemannian}
Let $F : M \to \tilde M$ present the $n$-manifold $M$ as a smooth immersion in the
$(n+1)$-manifold $\tilde M$, let $N$ be a family of ambient vectors along $M$ that varies
smoothly, and let $(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ be a smooth local frame for $TM$ over an open set $u$.
Then every member of the adapted family $\bigl(N, dF E_1, \ldots, dF E_n\bigr)$ is a smooth
section of $F^* T\tilde M$ over $u$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:smooth-normal-at,lem:pushforward-smooth}
The zeroth member is $N$, which is a smooth section by hypothesis. Each remaining member is a
pushforward $dF(E_i)$ of a smooth vector field, hence a smooth section of $F^* T\tilde M$ by
Lemma \ref{lem:pushforward-smooth}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Smoothness of the Value on a Frame]
\label{lem:normal-restrict-frame-smooth}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.contMDiffAt_normalRestrict_frame}
\leanok
\uses{def:smooth-normal-at,lem:adapted-frame-smooth,prop:oriented-orthonormal-frames,prop:volume-form-determinant,def:interior-multiplication,def:smooth-orientation,lem:ambient-tangent-bundle-riemannian,lem:pullback-comp-section}
Let $(\tilde M, \tilde g)$ be an oriented Riemannian $(n+1)$-manifold, let $F : M \to \tilde M$
present the $n$-manifold $M$ as a smooth immersion, let $N$ be a family of ambient vectors along
$M$ that varies smoothly, and let $(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ be a smooth local frame for $TM$ over an
open set $u$. Then
\[
  x \longmapsto \bigl((N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x(E_1|_x, \ldots, E_n|_x)
    = dV_{\tilde g}|_{F(x)}\bigl(N_x, dF_x E_1|_x, \ldots, dF_x E_n|_x\bigr)
\]
is a smooth real-valued function on $u$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{lem:adapted-frame-smooth,prop:oriented-orthonormal-frames,prop:volume-form-determinant,lem:pullback-comp-section,lem:ambient-tangent-bundle-riemannian}
Smoothness is local, so fix $x_0 \in u$. By Proposition \ref{prop:oriented-orthonormal-frames}
there is an open neighbourhood $w$ of $F(x_0)$ in $\tilde M$ carrying a smooth local frame
$(Z_0, \ldots, Z_n)$ for $T\tilde M$ that is orthonormal and positively oriented at every point
of $w$. Put $v = u \cap F^{-1}(w)$, an open neighbourhood of $x_0$.

For $x \in v$ the frame $(Z_a)$ is orthonormal and positively oriented at $F(x)$, so Proposition
\ref{prop:volume-form-determinant} gives, for any $v_0, \ldots, v_n \in T_{F(x)}\tilde M$,
\[
  dV_{\tilde g}|_{F(x)}(v_0, \ldots, v_n)
    = \det\bigl[\tilde g_{F(x)}(Z_a|_{F(x)}, v_b)\bigr]_{a,b}.
\]
Applying this to the adapted family $(W_0, \ldots, W_n) = \bigl(N, dF E_1, \ldots, dF E_n\bigr)$,
the function in question equals, on $v$,
\[
  x \longmapsto \det\bigl[\tilde g_{F(x)}\bigl(Z_a|_{F(x)}, W_b(x)\bigr)\bigr]_{a,b}.
\]
Each $x \mapsto Z_a|_{F(x)}$ is a smooth section of $F^* T\tilde M$ by Lemma
\ref{lem:pullback-comp-section}, and each $W_b$ is one by Lemma \ref{lem:adapted-frame-smooth}.
The metric of $F^* T\tilde M$ varies smoothly by Lemma
\ref{lem:ambient-tangent-bundle-riemannian}, so each matrix entry is a smooth function of
$x \in v$. A determinant is a polynomial in its entries, so the displayed function is smooth on
$v$, and in particular at $x_0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Negating a Frame Member Negates the Value]
\label{lem:normal-restrict-neg-member}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.normalRestrict_negMember}
\leanok
\uses{def:interior-multiplication,def:unit-normal}
In the situation of Proposition \ref{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-formula}, let
$(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ be a family of vectors in $T_x M$ and let $i_0$ be an index. Then
\[
  \bigl((N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x(E_1, \ldots, -E_{i_0}, \ldots, E_n)
    = - \bigl((N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x(E_1, \ldots, E_{i_0}, \ldots, E_n).
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
$\bigl((N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x$ is an alternating $n$-form on $T_x M$, hence
linear in each argument separately.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[The Induced Orientation is Smooth]
\label{prop:hypersurface-orientable-of-normal}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.isSmoothOrientation_inducedOrientation}
\leanok
\uses{def:induced-orientation,def:smooth-unit-normal-field,def:smooth-orientation,lem:normal-restrict-frame-smooth,lem:frame-neg-member,lem:normal-restrict-neg-member,lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation,prop:existence-orthonormal-frames,def:interior-multiplication,lem:adapted-frame-ambient-basis,lem:induced-orientation-characterization}
Let $(\tilde M, \tilde g)$ be an oriented Riemannian $(n+1)$-manifold with $n \geq 1$, let
$F : M \to \tilde M$ present the $n$-manifold $M$ as a smooth immersion, let $g$ be a metric on
$M$ that $F$ preserves, and let $N$ be a smooth global unit normal field for $M$. Then the
induced orientation of $M$ is smooth. In particular, $M$ is orientable.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:induced-orientation,lem:normal-restrict-frame-smooth,lem:frame-neg-member,lem:normal-restrict-neg-member,lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation,prop:existence-orthonormal-frames}
Fix $p \in M$. By Proposition \ref{prop:existence-orthonormal-frames} there is an open
neighbourhood $u$ of $p$ carrying a smooth $g$-orthonormal local frame $(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ for
$TM$. Consider
\[
  s(x) = \bigl((N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x(E_1|_x, \ldots, E_n|_x),
  \qquad x \in u .
\]
By Lemma \ref{lem:normal-restrict-frame-smooth} the function $s$ is smooth on $u$, hence
continuous. It never vanishes: by Definition \ref{def:induced-orientation} the form
$\bigl((N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x$ is a nonzero alternating $n$-form on $T_x M$, and
a nonzero alternating $n$-form on an $n$-dimensional space does not vanish on a basis, $(E_i|_x)$
being one. Moreover, by Lemma \ref{lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation}, $(E_i|_x)$ induces the
induced orientation of $M$ at $x$ if and only if $s(x) > 0$.

Since $s$ is continuous and $s(p) \neq 0$, exactly one of the following holds.

If $s(p) > 0$, then $u' = u \cap s^{-1}\bigl((0,\infty)\bigr)$ is an open neighbourhood of $p$, and
on it $(E_i)$ is a smooth local frame inducing the induced orientation at every point.

If $s(p) < 0$, then $u' = u \cap s^{-1}\bigl((-\infty,0)\bigr)$ is an open neighbourhood of $p$.
Because $n \geq 1$ there is an index $i_0$, and by Lemma \ref{lem:frame-neg-member} the family
$(E_i')$ obtained from $(E_i)$ by replacing $E_{i_0}$ with $-E_{i_0}$ is again a smooth local
frame over $u'$. By Lemma \ref{lem:normal-restrict-neg-member} its value satisfies
$\bigl((N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x(E_1'|_x, \ldots, E_n'|_x) = -s(x) > 0$ for every
$x \in u'$, so $(E_i')$ induces the induced orientation at every point of $u'$.

In both cases $p$ has an open neighbourhood carrying a smooth local frame that is positively
oriented for the induced orientation throughout. As $p$ was arbitrary, the induced orientation is
smooth.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
\label{rem:hypersurface-orientation-dimension}
\uses{prop:hypersurface-orientable-of-normal,def:smooth-orientation,def:induced-orientation}
The hypothesis $n \geq 1$ in Proposition \ref{prop:hypersurface-orientable-of-normal} cannot be
dropped. A smooth orientation is by Definition \ref{def:smooth-orientation} one realized near each
point by a positively oriented smooth local frame; a $0$-manifold admits only the empty frame,
whose orientation is the ray of the constant $1$. But $T_x M$ carries two orientations even when
$n = 0$, and for a $0$-manifold immersed in a $1$-manifold the induced orientation is the ray of
the number $dV_{\tilde g}(N_x) = \pm 1$, which may be $-1$. In that case the induced orientation
is not realized by any frame, though $M$ is of course still orientable.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Hypersurface Volume Form: the Sufficiency Half]
\label{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-if}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.exists_smoothOrientation_volumeForm_eq_normalRestrict}
\leanok
\uses{prop:hypersurface-orientable-of-normal,prop:hypersurface-volume-form-induced,def:induced-orientation,def:smooth-unit-normal-field,def:smooth-orientation,def:interior-multiplication}
Let $(\tilde M, \tilde g)$ be an oriented Riemannian $(n+1)$-manifold with $n \geq 1$, let
$F : M \to \tilde M$ present the $n$-manifold $M$ as a smooth immersion, let $g$ be a metric on
$M$ that $F$ preserves, and suppose $M$ admits a smooth global unit normal field $N$. Then $M$ is
orientable, and it carries a smooth orientation for which
\[
  dV_g = (N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde{g}})|_M. \tag{2.17}
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{prop:hypersurface-orientable-of-normal,prop:hypersurface-volume-form-induced}
Take the induced orientation of $M$. It is smooth by Proposition
\ref{prop:hypersurface-orientable-of-normal}, so $M$ is orientable, and (2.17) holds for it by
Proposition \ref{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-induced}.
\end{proof}

Proposition \ref{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-if} produces an orientation from a normal. The
converse produces a normal from an orientation, and rests on the fact that a hypersurface has
\emph{exactly two} unit normals at each point, of which the orientation selects one.

\begin{lemma}[A Hypersurface Has Exactly Two Unit Normals at Each Point]
\label{lem:two-unit-normals}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.eq_or_eq_neg_of_isUnitNormalVecAt}
\leanok
\uses{def:unit-normal,lem:normal-space-orthonormal-frame,def:metric-preserving}
Let $F : M \to \tilde M$ present the $n$-manifold $M$ as a smooth immersion in the Riemannian
$(n+1)$-manifold $(\tilde M, \tilde g)$, let $x \in M$, and suppose the normal space $N_x M$ is
the line spanned by a unit normal $w_0$. Then every unit normal at $x$ is $w_0$ or $-w_0$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:unit-normal}
A unit normal $w$ lies in $N_x M = \mathbb{R} \cdot w_0$, so $w = c\, w_0$ for some
$c \in \mathbb{R}$. Then
\[
  1 = \langle w, w \rangle_{\tilde g} = c^2 \langle w_0, w_0 \rangle_{\tilde g} = c^2,
\]
so $c = \pm 1$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[The Normal Space of a Hypersurface Is a Line]
\label{lem:pointwise-unit-normal-span}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.exists_isUnitNormalVecAt_span}
\leanok
\uses{def:unit-normal,lem:normal-space-orthonormal-frame}
In the situation of Lemma \ref{lem:two-unit-normals}, every $x \in M$ admits a unit normal $w_0$
with $N_x M = \mathbb{R} \cdot w_0$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{lem:normal-space-orthonormal-frame}
By Lemma \ref{lem:normal-space-orthonormal-frame} some neighbourhood of $x$ carries
$\dim \tilde M - \dim M$ smooth sections whose values at each of its points form an orthonormal
basis of the normal space. Here $\dim \tilde M - \dim M = 1$, so there is exactly one such
section; its value $w_0$ at $x$ is a unit normal and spans $N_x M$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Negating the Normal Negates the Contracted Form]
\label{lem:normal-restrict-neg-normal}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.normalRestrictVec_neg}
\leanok
\uses{def:interior-multiplication,def:unit-normal,def:volume-form-pointwise}
In the situation of Lemma \ref{lem:two-unit-normals}, for every $w \in T_{F(x)}\tilde M$,
\[
  \bigl(((-w) \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x = -\bigl((w \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x .
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
The contracted form places $w$ in the first slot of $dV_{\tilde g}$, and $dV_{\tilde g}$ is
multilinear, so negating that slot negates the value. No orthogonality, unit length or continuity
is used.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[A Basis Realizing a Prescribed Orientation]
\label{lem:basis-realizing-orientation}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.exists_basis_orientation_eq}
\leanok
\uses{lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation}
Let $M$ be an $n$-manifold with $n \geq 1$, let $o$ be a pointwise orientation of $M$ and let
$x \in M$. Then $T_x M$ has a basis that is positively oriented for $o(x)$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
Take any basis of $T_x M$. Its orientation is either $o(x)$, in which case it serves, or the
opposite one, in which case negating one of its members — possible because $n \geq 1$ — reverses
its orientation and produces the required basis.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[A Unit Normal Inducing a Given Orientation]
\label{def:oriented-unit-normal}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.IsOrientedUnitNormalVecAt}
\leanok
\uses{def:unit-normal,def:interior-multiplication,def:induced-orientation,lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation}
Let $o$ be a pointwise orientation of $M$ and $x \in M$. A unit normal $w$ at $x$
\emph{induces $o$ at $x$} if
$\bigl((w \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x(b_1,\ldots,b_n) > 0$ for every basis
$(b_1,\ldots,b_n)$ of $T_x M$ that is positively oriented for $o(x)$.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[One Basis Suffices]
\label{lem:oriented-unit-normal-iff-pos}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.isOrientedUnitNormalVecAt_iff_pos}
\leanok
\uses{def:oriented-unit-normal,lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation,def:unit-normal,def:metric-preserving,lem:adapted-frame-ambient-basis}
In the situation of Definition \ref{def:oriented-unit-normal}, let $b$ be one basis of $T_x M$
that is positively oriented for $o(x)$. Then the unit normal $w$ induces $o$ at $x$ if and only if
$\bigl((w \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x(b) > 0$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation}
The form $\bigl((w \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x$ is a nonzero $n$-form, so by Lemma
\ref{lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation} its positivity on $b$ says exactly that its ray equals
the orientation determined by $b$, which is $o(x)$. That is a statement about rays and mentions no
basis, so by the same lemma it implies positivity on every other basis positively oriented for
$o(x)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[An Orientation Selects a Unit Normal]
\label{prop:existsunique-oriented-unit-normal}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.existsUnique_isOrientedUnitNormalVecAt}
\leanok
\uses{def:oriented-unit-normal,lem:two-unit-normals,lem:pointwise-unit-normal-span,lem:normal-restrict-neg-normal,lem:basis-realizing-orientation,lem:oriented-unit-normal-iff-pos,def:unit-normal,def:metric-preserving}
Let $(\tilde M, \tilde g)$ be an oriented Riemannian $(n+1)$-manifold with $n \geq 1$, let
$F : M \to \tilde M$ present the $n$-manifold $M$ as a smooth immersion, let $g$ be a metric on
$M$ that $F$ preserves, and let $o$ be a pointwise orientation of $M$. Then each $x \in M$ has
exactly one unit normal inducing $o$ at $x$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{lem:two-unit-normals,lem:pointwise-unit-normal-span,lem:normal-restrict-neg-normal,lem:basis-realizing-orientation,lem:oriented-unit-normal-iff-pos}
By Lemma \ref{lem:pointwise-unit-normal-span} there is a unit normal $w_0$ at $x$ spanning
$N_x M$, and by Lemma \ref{lem:two-unit-normals} the only unit normals at $x$ are $\pm w_0$. By
Lemma \ref{lem:basis-realizing-orientation} fix a basis $b$ of $T_x M$ positively oriented for
$o(x)$, and set $t = \bigl((w_0 \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x(b)$. As in Proposition
\ref{prop:hypersurface-orientable-of-normal}, $t \neq 0$, because a nonzero $n$-form does not
vanish on a basis.

If $t > 0$ then $w_0$ induces $o$ at $x$ by Lemma \ref{lem:oriented-unit-normal-iff-pos}, and
$-w_0$ does not, since by Lemma \ref{lem:normal-restrict-neg-normal} its value on $b$ is $-t < 0$.
If $t < 0$ the roles are exchanged. Either way exactly one of $\pm w_0$ induces $o$ at $x$.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[The Unit Normal Determined by an Orientation]
\label{def:unit-normal-of-orientation}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.unitNormalOfOrientation}
\leanok
\uses{prop:existsunique-oriented-unit-normal,def:oriented-unit-normal}
In the situation of Proposition \ref{prop:existsunique-oriented-unit-normal}, the
\emph{unit normal determined by $o$} assigns to each $x \in M$ the unique unit normal at $x$
inducing $o$ at $x$. This is a global normal field, defined with no choices beyond the sign that
$o$ itself fixes.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[The Normal Determined by an Orientation Is Smooth]
\label{prop:unit-normal-of-orientation-smooth}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.isSmoothNormalField_unitNormalOfOrientation}
\leanok
\uses{def:unit-normal-of-orientation,def:smooth-unit-normal-field,def:smooth-orientation,lem:normal-space-orthonormal-frame,lem:normal-restrict-frame-smooth,lem:oriented-unit-normal-iff-pos,lem:normal-restrict-neg-normal,prop:existsunique-oriented-unit-normal,def:interior-multiplication}
In the situation of Proposition \ref{prop:existsunique-oriented-unit-normal}, suppose in addition
that $o$ is a smooth orientation of $M$ and that the orientation of $\tilde M$ is smooth. Then the
unit normal determined by $o$ is a smooth global unit normal field.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{lem:normal-space-orthonormal-frame,lem:normal-restrict-frame-smooth,lem:oriented-unit-normal-iff-pos,lem:normal-restrict-neg-normal,prop:existsunique-oriented-unit-normal}
Write $N$ for the unit normal determined by $o$ and fix $p \in M$. Because $o$ is smooth, some
open $u \ni p$ carries a smooth local frame $(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ of $TM$ that is positively
oriented for $o$ at every point of $u$. By Lemma \ref{lem:normal-space-orthonormal-frame} some
open $v \ni p$ carries a smooth local unit normal $W$. Put $c = u \cap v$ and
\[
  s(x) = \bigl((W \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x(E_1|_x, \ldots, E_n|_x), \qquad x \in c .
\]
By Lemma \ref{lem:normal-restrict-frame-smooth} $s$ is smooth on $c$, hence continuous, and it
never vanishes there, a nonzero $n$-form not vanishing on a basis.

By Lemma \ref{lem:oriented-unit-normal-iff-pos}, $W_x$ induces $o$ at $x \in c$ exactly when
$s(x) > 0$; and by Lemma \ref{lem:normal-restrict-neg-normal} the value of the form on $(E_i|_x)$
for $-W_x$ is $-s(x)$, so $-W_x$ induces $o$ at $x$ exactly when $s(x) < 0$. Since $s(p) \neq 0$,
one of these two cases holds on the open neighbourhood $c \cap s^{-1}\bigl((0,\infty)\bigr)$ or
$c \cap s^{-1}\bigl((-\infty,0)\bigr)$ of $p$; by the uniqueness in Proposition
\ref{prop:existsunique-oriented-unit-normal}, $N = W$ on the first and $N = -W$ on the second.
Both $W$ and $-W$ are smooth on $v$, so $N$ is smooth at $p$. As $p$ was arbitrary, $N$ is a
smooth global unit normal field.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Hypersurface Volume Form: the Necessity Half]
\label{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-only-if}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.exists_isSmoothNormalField_volumeForm_eq_normalRestrict}
\leanok
\uses{prop:unit-normal-of-orientation-smooth,def:unit-normal-of-orientation,prop:hypersurface-volume-form-induced,def:induced-orientation,lem:oriented-unit-normal-iff-pos,lem:basis-realizing-orientation,def:smooth-unit-normal-field,def:smooth-orientation,def:interior-multiplication}
Let $(\tilde M, \tilde g)$ be an oriented Riemannian $(n+1)$-manifold with $n \geq 1$, let
$F : M \to \tilde M$ present the $n$-manifold $M$ as a smooth immersion, let $g$ be a metric on
$M$ that $F$ preserves, and suppose $M$ carries a smooth orientation $o$. Then $M$ admits a
smooth global unit normal field $N$, and for it
\[
  dV_g = (N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde{g}})|_M. \tag{2.17}
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{prop:unit-normal-of-orientation-smooth,prop:hypersurface-volume-form-induced,lem:oriented-unit-normal-iff-pos,lem:basis-realizing-orientation}
Let $N$ be the unit normal determined by $o$; it is a smooth global unit normal field by
Proposition \ref{prop:unit-normal-of-orientation-smooth}. Its induced orientation is $o$ itself:
at each $x$, pick by Lemma \ref{lem:basis-realizing-orientation} a basis $b$ of $T_x M$ positively
oriented for $o(x)$; then $\bigl((N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M\bigr)_x(b) > 0$ because $N_x$
induces $o$ at $x$, so by Lemma \ref{lem:nonvanishing-top-form-orientation} the ray of that form
— which is by definition the induced orientation at $x$ — equals the orientation of $b$, namely
$o(x)$. Now (2.17) is Proposition \ref{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-induced} applied to $N$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}
\label{prop:hypersurface-volume-form}
\dcref{ch2:2.43}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.exists_isSmoothOrientation_iff_exists_isSmoothNormalField}
\leanok
\uses{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-formula,prop:hypersurface-volume-form-induced,prop:hypersurface-volume-form-if,prop:hypersurface-volume-form-only-if,prop:hypersurface-orientable-of-normal,prop:unit-normal-of-orientation-smooth,def:induced-orientation,def:smooth-unit-normal-field,def:unit-normal,def:interior-multiplication,lem:normal-space-orthonormal-frame,lem:induced-orientation-characterization}
Let $(\tilde M, \tilde g)$ be an oriented Riemannian $(n+1)$-manifold with $n \geq 1$, let
$F : M \to \tilde M$ present the $n$-manifold $M$ as a smooth immersion, and let $g$ be a metric
on $M$ that $F$ preserves — for instance the induced metric. Then $M$ is orientable if and only
if there exists a smooth global unit normal vector field $N$ for $M$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-if,prop:hypersurface-volume-form-only-if,prop:hypersurface-orientable-of-normal,prop:unit-normal-of-orientation-smooth,def:induced-orientation,def:smooth-unit-normal-field}
If $N$ is a smooth global unit normal field, then the orientation it induces (Definition
\ref{def:induced-orientation}) is smooth by Proposition
\ref{prop:hypersurface-orientable-of-normal}, so $M$ is orientable. Conversely, if $M$ carries a
smooth orientation $o$, then the unit normal determined by $o$ is a smooth global unit normal
field by Proposition \ref{prop:unit-normal-of-orientation-smooth}.
\end{proof}

In either direction the volume form is the contraction of the ambient one against the normal:
equation (2.17),
\[
  dV_g = (N \lrcorner dV_{\tilde g})|_M ,
\]
holds for the orientation and normal that the respective direction produces. That is
Proposition \ref{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-if} for a given normal and Proposition
\ref{prop:hypersurface-volume-form-only-if} for a given orientation.

When $M$ is not orientable, we can still define integrals of functions, but now we have to use \emph{densities} instead of differential forms (see pp.~405--406).

\subsection{The density of an inner product space}

A density on a vector space is the unoriented analogue of a top-degree form: it assigns an
unsigned volume to an $n$-tuple of vectors, and consequently transforms by $|\det|$ rather than
by $\det$. Because no sign is involved, no orientation is needed anywhere in this subsection,
and that is precisely what makes Proposition \ref{prop:riemannian-density} available on every
Riemannian manifold rather than only on the orientable ones.

\begin{definition}[Density of a Vector Space]
\label{def:density-vector-space}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.IsDensity}
\leanok
Let $V$ be an $n$-dimensional real vector space. A \emph{density} on $V$ is a function
$\mu : V^n \to \mathbb{R}$ such that
\begin{equation}
\mu(f v_1, \ldots, f v_n) = |\det f| \, \mu(v_1, \ldots, v_n)
\tag{B.14}
\end{equation}
for every linear map $f : V \to V$ and all $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in V$. A density is
\emph{positive} if $\mu(v_1, \ldots, v_n) > 0$ whenever $(v_1, \ldots, v_n)$ is a basis of $V$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[The Density of an Inner Product Space]
\label{def:density-pointwise}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.densityL}
\leanok
Let $V$ be an $n$-dimensional real inner product space. For $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in V$ set
\[
|v_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge v_n| := \sqrt{\det \bigl( \langle v_i, v_j \rangle \bigr)_{i,j=1}^{n}},
\]
the square root of the determinant of the Gram matrix of $(v_1, \ldots, v_n)$. The Gram matrix
is positive semidefinite, so its determinant is nonnegative and the square root is defined.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[The Determinant Formula for the Density]
\label{prop:density-abs-det}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.densityL_eq_abs_det}
\leanok
\uses{def:density-pointwise}
Let $V$ be an $n$-dimensional real inner product space, let $(e_1, \ldots, e_n)$ be any
orthonormal basis of $V$, and let $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in V$. Then
\[
|v_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge v_n| = \bigl| \det \bigl( \langle e_i, v_j \rangle \bigr)_{i,j=1}^{n} \bigr|.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:density-pointwise}
Write $M = (\langle e_i, v_j \rangle)_{i,j}$. Expanding each $v_j$ in the orthonormal basis gives
$v_j = \sum_k \langle e_k, v_j \rangle e_k$, so
\[
\langle v_i, v_j \rangle
= \Bigl\langle \sum_k \langle e_k, v_i \rangle e_k, \; \sum_l \langle e_l, v_j \rangle e_l \Bigr\rangle
= \sum_k \langle e_k, v_i \rangle \langle e_k, v_j \rangle,
\]
by orthonormality of $(e_k)$; that is, the Gram matrix of $(v_1, \ldots, v_n)$ equals
$M^{\mathsf{T}} M$. Hence
$\det (\langle v_i, v_j \rangle) = \det(M^{\mathsf{T}}) \det(M) = (\det M)^2$, and taking the
square root gives $\sqrt{(\det M)^2} = |\det M|$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[The Density of an Orthonormal Basis]
\label{prop:density-value-one}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.densityL_apply_orthonormalBasis}
\leanok
\uses{prop:density-abs-det}
Let $V$ be an $n$-dimensional real inner product space and let $(e_1, \ldots, e_n)$ be an
orthonormal basis of $V$. Then $|e_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge e_n| = 1$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{prop:density-abs-det}
Apply Proposition \ref{prop:density-abs-det} with $v_i = e_i$. The matrix
$(\langle e_i, e_j \rangle)_{i,j}$ is the identity matrix by orthonormality, and its determinant
is $1$, so the density is $|1| = 1$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[The Transformation Law]
\label{prop:density-transformation-law}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.densityL_comp}
\leanok
\uses{prop:density-abs-det,def:density-vector-space}
Let $V$ be an $n$-dimensional real inner product space, let $f : V \to V$ be linear and let
$v_1, \ldots, v_n \in V$. Then
\[
|f v_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge f v_n| = |\det f| \cdot |v_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge v_n|.
\]
In particular $|{\cdot} \wedge \cdots \wedge {\cdot}|$ is a density on $V$ in the sense of
Definition \ref{def:density-vector-space}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{prop:density-abs-det}
Fix an orthonormal basis $(e_1, \ldots, e_n)$ of $V$ and let $A = (\langle e_i, f e_k \rangle)_{i,k}$
be the matrix of $f$ in that basis, so that $\det A = \det f$. Expanding $v_j$ in the basis and
using linearity of $f$,
\[
\langle e_i, f v_j \rangle
= \Bigl\langle e_i, \; f \Bigl( \sum_k \langle e_k, v_j \rangle e_k \Bigr) \Bigr\rangle
= \sum_k \langle e_i, f e_k \rangle \langle e_k, v_j \rangle,
\]
so the matrix of $(f v_1, \ldots, f v_n)$ against $(e_i)$ is $A \cdot M$, where
$M = (\langle e_i, v_j \rangle)_{i,j}$. By Proposition \ref{prop:density-abs-det} applied twice,
\[
|f v_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge f v_n| = |\det(AM)| = |\det A| \, |\det M|
= |\det f| \cdot |v_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge v_n|. \qedhere
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Positivity of the Density]
\label{prop:density-positive}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.densityL_pos}
\leanok
\uses{def:density-pointwise}
Let $V$ be an $n$-dimensional real inner product space and let $(v_1, \ldots, v_n)$ be linearly
independent. Then $|v_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge v_n| > 0$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:density-pointwise}
The Gram matrix of a linearly independent family is positive definite: for $c \neq 0$ the vector
$w = \sum_j c_j v_j$ is nonzero, and $c^{\mathsf{T}} (\langle v_i, v_j \rangle) c = \langle w, w \rangle > 0$.
A positive definite matrix has positive determinant, so the square root defining
$|v_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge v_n|$ is a square root of a positive number.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Fibrewise Uniqueness of the Density]
\label{prop:density-uniqueness-pointwise}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.densityL_unique}
\leanok
\uses{def:density-vector-space,prop:density-transformation-law,prop:density-value-one}
Let $V$ be an $n$-dimensional real inner product space, let $(e_1, \ldots, e_n)$ be an orthonormal
basis of $V$, and let $\mu$ be a density on $V$ with $\mu(e_1, \ldots, e_n) = 1$. Then
$\mu(v_1, \ldots, v_n) = |v_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge v_n|$ for all $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in V$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{prop:density-transformation-law,prop:density-value-one}
Let $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in V$ and let $f : V \to V$ be the unique linear map with $f e_i = v_i$ for
every $i$. By the transformation law (B.14) for $\mu$ and the hypothesis $\mu(e_1,\ldots,e_n) = 1$,
\[
\mu(v_1, \ldots, v_n) = \mu(f e_1, \ldots, f e_n) = |\det f| \, \mu(e_1, \ldots, e_n) = |\det f|.
\]
By Proposition \ref{prop:density-transformation-law} and Proposition \ref{prop:density-value-one}
the same computation gives
$|v_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge v_n| = |\det f| \cdot |e_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge e_n| = |\det f|$.
The two agree.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[The Density Is the Absolute Value of the Volume Form]
\label{prop:density-eq-abs-volume-form}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.densityL_eq_abs_volumeForm}
\leanok
\uses{def:density-pointwise,prop:volume-form-determinant}
Let $V$ be an $n$-dimensional real inner product space with $n > 0$, let $o$ be an orientation of
$V$, and let $\omega$ be the volume form of $(V, o)$. Then
$|v_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge v_n| = |\omega(v_1, \ldots, v_n)|$ for all $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in V$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{prop:density-abs-det}
Choose an orthonormal basis $(e_1, \ldots, e_n)$ of $V$ inducing $o$; this is possible because
$n > 0$. The determinant formula for the volume form gives
$\omega(v_1, \ldots, v_n) = \det (\langle e_i, v_j \rangle)_{i,j}$, while Proposition
\ref{prop:density-abs-det} gives
$|v_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge v_n| = |\det (\langle e_i, v_j \rangle)_{i,j}|$. Taking absolute values
of the former yields the latter.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Smooth densities and the Riemannian density}

\begin{definition}[Smooth Density]
\label{def:smooth-density}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.SmoothDensity}
\leanok
\uses{def:density-vector-space}
Let $M$ be a smooth $n$-manifold. A \emph{smooth density} on $M$ is a family $\mu$ assigning to
each $x \in M$ a density $\mu_x$ on $T_x M$, such that for every smooth local frame
$(Y_1, \ldots, Y_n)$ on an open set $u \subseteq M$ the function
$x \mapsto \mu_x(Y_1|_x, \ldots, Y_n|_x)$ is smooth on $u$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[The Riemannian Density, Pointwise]
\label{def:riemannian-density-pointwise}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.densityAt}
\leanok
\uses{def:density-pointwise,def:riemannian-metric}
Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian $n$-manifold. For $x \in M$ and $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in T_x M$ let
\[
\mu_x(v_1, \ldots, v_n) := \sqrt{\det \bigl( \langle v_i, v_j \rangle_g \bigr)_{i,j=1}^{n}}
\]
be the density of the inner product space $(T_x M, g_x)$ of Definition
\ref{def:density-pointwise}. No orientation of $M$ enters this definition.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Smoothness of the Riemannian Density]
\label{prop:density-smooth}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.RiemannianMetric.contMDiffOn_densityAt}
\leanok
\uses{def:riemannian-density-pointwise,prop:density-positive,lem:inner-product-vector-fields-smooth}
Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian $n$-manifold and let $(Y_1, \ldots, Y_n)$ be a smooth local frame on
an open set $u \subseteq M$. Then $x \mapsto \mu_x(Y_1|_x, \ldots, Y_n|_x)$ is smooth on $u$; that
is, $\mu$ is a smooth density.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:riemannian-density-pointwise,prop:density-positive,lem:inner-product-vector-fields-smooth}
The entries $x \mapsto \langle Y_i|_x, Y_j|_x \rangle_g$ of the Gram matrix are smooth on $u$,
being pairings of smooth vector fields under $g$. A determinant is a polynomial in the matrix
entries, so $x \mapsto \det (\langle Y_i|_x, Y_j|_x \rangle_g)$ is smooth on $u$. At every $x \in u$
the vectors $(Y_1|_x, \ldots, Y_n|_x)$ are linearly independent, so this determinant is strictly
positive by Proposition \ref{prop:density-positive}; since the square root is smooth away from
$0$, the composite $x \mapsto \sqrt{\det (\langle Y_i|_x, Y_j|_x \rangle_g)}$ is smooth on $u$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[The Riemannian Density]\label{prop:riemannian-density}\dcref{ch2:2.44}
\lean{LeeLib.Ch02.riemannian_density_existsUnique}
\leanok
\uses{def:smooth-density,def:riemannian-density-pointwise,prop:density-smooth,prop:density-transformation-law,prop:density-value-one,prop:density-uniqueness-pointwise,prop:density-positive,prop:existence-orthonormal-frames}
If $(M,g)$ is any Riemannian manifold, then there is a unique smooth positive density $\mu$ on $M$, called the \emph{Riemannian density}, with the property that
\begin{equation}
\mu(E_1,\ldots,E_n) = 1 \tag{2.18}
\end{equation}
for every local orthonormal frame $(E_i)$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\leanok
\uses{def:riemannian-density-pointwise,prop:density-smooth,prop:density-transformation-law,prop:density-value-one,prop:density-uniqueness-pointwise,prop:density-positive,prop:existence-orthonormal-frames}
\emph{Existence.} Take $\mu$ to be the family of Definition \ref{def:riemannian-density-pointwise}.
Each $\mu_x$ is a density on $T_x M$ by Proposition \ref{prop:density-transformation-law}, and
$\mu$ is smooth by Proposition \ref{prop:density-smooth}, so $\mu$ is a smooth density. If
$(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ is a local orthonormal frame on $u$ then $(E_1|_x, \ldots, E_n|_x)$ is an
orthonormal basis of $(T_x M, g_x)$ for each $x \in u$, so $\mu_x(E_1|_x, \ldots, E_n|_x) = 1$ by
Proposition \ref{prop:density-value-one}; this is (2.18). It is positive by Proposition
\ref{prop:density-positive}, since the values of a frame are linearly independent.

\emph{Uniqueness.} Let $\nu$ be a smooth density satisfying (2.18) and let $x \in M$. By
Proposition \ref{prop:existence-orthonormal-frames} there are a neighbourhood $u$ of $x$ and a
local orthonormal frame $(E_1, \ldots, E_n)$ on $u$. Then $(E_1|_x, \ldots, E_n|_x)$ is an
orthonormal basis of $T_x M$ and $\nu_x(E_1|_x, \ldots, E_n|_x) = 1$ by (2.18). Since $\nu_x$ is a
density on $T_x M$ taking the value $1$ on an orthonormal basis, Proposition
\ref{prop:density-uniqueness-pointwise} gives $\nu_x = \mu_x$. As $x$ was arbitrary, $\nu = \mu$.
\end{proof}

\begin{exercise}\label{exer:riemannian-density-formula}\dcref{ch2:2.45}
\uses{prop:riemannian-density}
Prove this proposition by showing that $\mu$ can be defined in terms of any local orthonormal frame by
\[
\mu = |\varepsilon^1 \wedge \cdots \wedge \varepsilon^n|.
\]
\end{exercise}

Let $(M,g)$ be a Riemannian manifold (with or without boundary). If $M$ is oriented and $dV_g$ is its Riemannian volume form, then its Riemannian density is easily seen to be equal to $|dV_g|$. On the other hand, the Riemannian density is defined whether $M$ is oriented or not. It is customary to denote the Riemannian density by the same notation $dV_g$ that we use for the Riemannian volume form, and to specify when necessary whether the notation refers to a density or a form. In either case, we can define the integral of a compactly supported smooth function $f: M \to \mathbb{R}$ as $\int_M f\, dV_g$. This is to be interpreted as the integral of a density when $M$ is nonorientable; when $M$ is orientable, it can be interpreted either as the integral of a density
or as the integral of an $n$-form (with respect to some choice of orientation), because
both give the same result.

\section{The Divergence and the Laplacian}

In advanced calculus, you have undoubtedly been introduced to three important
differential operators involving vector fields on $\mathbb{R}^3$: the \emph{gradient} (which takes real-valued functions to vector fields), \emph{divergence} (vector fields to functions), and \emph{curl}
(vector fields to vector fields). We have already described how the gradient operator
can be generalized to Riemannian manifolds (see equation (2.14)); now we can show
that the divergence operator also generalizes easily to that setting. Problem 2-27
describes a similar, but more limited, generalization of the curl.

Suppose $(M, g)$ is an oriented Riemannian $n$-manifold with or without boundary,
